## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical reaction kinetics. The rate law typically depends on powers of concentration, but may involve more complex mechanisms like reversible reactions, autocatalysis, or Michaelis-Menten type saturation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalytic reaction with finite reagent)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturating kinetics)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized with equilibrium shift)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Cubic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A (polynomial rate law from complex mechanism)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence → dA/dt = c*A^n indicates an nth-order elementary reaction or apparent order from a complex mechanism
- Linear dependence on A with nonzero intercept → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium, dA/dt = c0*A + c1
- Product of A and (c-A) terms → autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics where both reactant and product concentrations matter
- Rational functions of A (A in both numerator and denominator) → enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed reactions with adsorption/saturation
- Explicit time dependence in rate expression → non-isothermal conditions, photochemical reactions, or catalyst deactivation
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel reaction pathways or complex mechanisms with multiple elementary steps
- Square root or fractional powers of A → dissociative adsorption or chain reaction mechanisms where intermediates are in quasi-steady-state
- Negative coefficients on A terms → consumption/depletion of reactant (expected for reactant disappearance)
- A*(1-A) or A*(c-A) structure → conservation constraint where total concentration is fixed and product formation feeds back
